         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202310426-sec-0090">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="smll202310426-sec-0090-title">4.1 Converted Metal Phosphides for Sodium Storage</h3>
            
            <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202310426-sec-0100">
               
               <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section3" id="smll202310426-sec-0100-title">4.1.1 Co-P</h4>
               
               <p>There are many different stoichiometric ratios of cobalt phosphide, such as Co<sub>2</sub>P, CoP, CoP<sub>2</sub>, and so on.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0062" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0062_R_d140478325e2774" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 62 - Adv. Energy Mater.">62</a>, <a href="#smll202310426-bib-0144" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0144_R_d140478325e2774" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 144 - Eur. J. Inorg. Chem.">144</a>-<a href="#smll202310426-bib-0146" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0146_R_d140478325e2774" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 146 - Appl. Surf. Sci.">146</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Wu et&nbsp;al. synthesized separated mesoporous np-Co(OH)<sub><i>x</i></sub>/Co<sub>2</sub>P by neutral salt solution-mediated electrochemical dealloying.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0147" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0147_R_d140478325e2785" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 147 - Adv. Mater.">147</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Its initial reversible capacity reaches ≈254, 207, 176, 154, 105, 80.5, and 65.8&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.049, 0.122, 0.244, 0.49, 1.22, 2.44, and 4.88&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. As the cycle progresses, the capacity also increases. During the preparation process, the in situ Co(OH)<sub><i>x</i></sub> precipitation and trace Co<sub>3</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub> can be uniformly deposited on the 3D bicontinuous ligaments of the in situ mesoporous Co<sub>2</sub>P framework. Thus, on the one hand, this binder-free and collector-free nanostructured electrode is loaded with a large number of active materials (packing density &gt; 3.0&nbsp;g&nbsp;cm<sup>−3</sup>) to meet the capacity that can be achieved in practical applications. On the other hand, due to the conductivity of Co<sub>2</sub>P matrix, well-structured Co(OH)<sub><i>x</i></sub>-Co<sub>2</sub>P heterostructure, and highly developed nanopore structure, it not only exhibits excellent hybrid conductivity but also enables fast electron and ion transfer simultaneously. Moreover, it has high mechanical stability and can reduce the volume change during charging and discharging. Ren et&nbsp;al. synthesized a CoP@C composite with a hollow dodecahedral structure.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0124" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0124_R_d140478325e2816" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 124 - Rare Met.">124</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The unique hollow carbon framework (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#smll202310426-fig-0005">5a</a>) serves multiple crucial functions in this context. First, it facilitates a high-speed path for electron and ion transport for the CoP material. Additionally, it enables rapid sodium storage kinetics, contributing to efficient energy storage and release. Furthermore, the framework accommodates large volume expansion, which is essential for stabilizing the electrode structure and maintaining the specific cycle capacity over multiple charge and discharge cycles. As a result, CoP@C composite can exhibit an ultra-high magnification capability of 105&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at a current density of 30&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202310426-fig-0005">5b</a>) and have a long cycle life. Jiang et&nbsp;al. synthesized CoP@N-HP/CT by the epitaxial growth of carbon nanotubes using the strategies of MOF coating, carbonization, oxidation-phosphating, etc.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0148" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0148_R_d140478325e2835" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 148 - Chem. Eng. J.">148</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The synthesis process and the sodium storage process of CoP@N-HP/CT are shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202310426-fig-0005">5c</a>. The material immobilizes a layered hollow superstructure composed of CoP nanoparticles on an N-doped carbon polyhedron framework. Due to the well-designed layered hollow superstructure, the CoP@N-HP/CT composite has long cycle stability (more than 2500 cycles) and good rate capability as SIBs anode. CoP@N-HP/CT composite has high capacitance contribution, fast diffusion rate of sodium ions, and remarkable electrochemical properties. Li et&nbsp;al. designed a coral-like CoP with an N, P co-doped carbon shell on carbon paper derived from a metal–organic framework shell.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0149" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0149_R_d140478325e2844" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 149 - ChemElectroChem">149</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The optimized coral-like CoP with N, P co-doped carbon shell on carbon paper at 200&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> can provide a high reversible capacity of 318.9&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 150 cycles. Even when the current density is 1000&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 1000 cycles, it still maintains a high discharge capacity of 191.2&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. Electrochemical analysis shows that the independent hierarchical structure is beneficial to chemical mass diffusion and electron conduction. N, P co-doped carbon shell not only maintains the structural integrity of the nanomaterials, but also introduces vacancies in the electrode material, providing abundant unsaturated site coordination for sodium storage. Huang et&nbsp;al. designed highly separated CoP nanoparticles encased in a 3D hollow nitrogen-doped carbon network (CoP/HNC composite) by polymerizing and subsequently in situ phosphorization polydopamine (PDA) on ZIF-67.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0090" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0090_R_d140478325e2858" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 90 - Electrochim. Acta">90</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Ultrafine CoP nanoparticles (10&nbsp;±&nbsp;2&nbsp;nm) are decorated in an N-doped carbon polyhedral shell, forming the porous 3D hollow structure. Owing to its unique structure, the CoP/HNC electrode provides a highly reversible long-cycle life capacity of 223&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 500&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 700 cycles (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202310426-fig-0005">5d</a>). DFT simulation shows that Na atoms are tightly bound to the CoP surface and significantly enriched near the CoP surface, which is conducive to the storage of Na ions in the composite. Sun et&nbsp;al. designed and synthesized a multi-layered Spanish dagger-shaped CoP nanosheet decorated with a carbon sponge (CoP/CS).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0150" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0150_R_d140478325e2871" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 150 - Electrochim. Acta">150</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The synthesis process is shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202310426-fig-0005">5e</a>. The structure consists of a first-order ultra-fine CoP nanorod, second-order micro-size flower, third-order flower/dendritic carbon skeleton, and four-stage electrode with the dynamic spatial 3D network. This unique structure offers several advantages. First, it limits the volume expansion and self-aggregation of CoP, thereby significantly enhancing the cycle performance of the material. Additionally, it plays a crucial role in reducing the transport length of Na<sup>+</sup>, further contributing to the overall property of the material. This unique structure not only limits the volume expansion and self-aggregation of CoP but also reduces the transport length of Na<sup>+</sup>. The CoP/CS composite has a capacity of 0.834&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;cm<sup>−2</sup> after 50 cycles. The capacity is 0.514&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;cm<sup>−2</sup> after 900 cycles at 1&nbsp;mA&nbsp;cm<sup>−2</sup>, showing excellent cyclic stability. Liu et&nbsp;al. for the first time synthesized homogeneous CoP nanoparticles encased in N-doped carbon (CoP/NC) microspheres by simultaneous carbonization and phosphorization of Co-salen composite microspheres.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0125" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0125_R_d140478325e2890" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 125 - Inorg. Chem.">125</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The higher degree of disorder of carbon provides more active sites for Na<sup>+</sup> storage. At the same time, the presence of N-doped carbon is very effective for improving the electrical conductivity of the material and reducing the stress caused by the volume expansion of the material. CoP nanoparticles dispersed in carbon provide more reactive sites, which improves the storage performance of sodium. The CoP nanoparticles are confined to the carbon skeleton, effectively preventing the accumulation of the active material and thus inhibiting the capacity decay during the cycle. After 100 cycles, the CoP/NC microsphere has a capacity of 373&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. Even after 2000 cycles at 2&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, a capacity of 195&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> can be achieved. Chang et&nbsp;al. synthesized S-CoP@NPC with a hollow nanotube structure (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202310426-fig-0005">5f</a>) consisting of nitrogen-doped porous carbon coated with sulfur-doped cobalt phosphide (S-CoP) nanoparticles by hydrothermal method and vulcanization.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0151" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0151_R_d140478325e2909" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 151 - J. Colloid Interface Sci.">151</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The material has stable cyclic performance, showing a specific discharge capacity of 230&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 370 cycles at 0.2&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. In addition, it also shows a good rate performance. The specific discharge capacity can reach 143&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. Even if the current density is restored to 0.2&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, the specific discharge capacity can be restored to 213&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>.</p>
               
               <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
                  <figure class="figure" id="smll202310426-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/6e80982a-1300-44a1-860d-8ce576aee372/smll202310426-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>

                        </div>
                        <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) TEM image of CoP@C composites. Reproduced with permission. Reproduced with permission.<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0124" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0124_R_d140478325e2952" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 124 - Rare Met.">124</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Copyright 2022, Springer Nature. c) The synthesis process and the sodium storage process of CoP@N-HP/CT. Acta">106</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Copyright 2022, Elsevier.</div>
                     </figcaption>
                  </figure>
               </section>
               <p>Increasing the content of phosphorus in metal phosphide can improve its charge storage capacity. For example, the theoretical sodium storage capacity of CoP<sub>2</sub> is 1330&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, which is significantly higher than CoP (893&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0106" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0106_R_d140478325e3007" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 106 - Electrochim. Acta">106</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The CoP<sub>2</sub>@C synthesized by Hu et&nbsp;al. has good electrochemical performance.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0106" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0106_R_d140478325e3015" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 106 - Electrochim. Acta">106</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The intercalation reaction mechanism of the material is shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202310426-fig-0005">5g,h</a>. The electrochemical properties of CoP<sub>2</sub>@C-0.5 are excellent in terms of high-rate performance and cycle stability. CoP<sub>2</sub>@C-0.5 has a discharge capacity of 563&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> on the second cycle. At a current of 500&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, the discharge capacity at the 1000th cycle is 406&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. And the corresponding capacity retention rate is 72.1%. CoP<sub>2</sub>@C-0.5 shows a higher reversible capacity. After several cycles, the coulomb efficiency reaches 100%. After cycling, a thick SEI layer with a thickness between 40 and 50&nbsp;nm is observed on the CoP<sub>2</sub>@C-0.5 surface. The SEI film forms uniformly and maintains a good initial rod morphology in CoP<sub>2</sub>@C-0.5. The agglomeration of CoP<sub>2</sub> particles is one of the reasons for the rapid capacity decay.</p>
               </section>
            
            <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202310426-sec-0110">
               
               <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section3" id="smll202310426-sec-0110-title">4.1.2 Fe-P</h4>
               
               <p>Recently, iron phosphide (Fe<sub>2</sub>P, FeP, FeP<sub>2</sub>, and FeP<sub>4</sub>) has been investigated as anode materials for SIBs.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0152" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0152_R_d140478325e3058" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 152 - ACS Sustainable Chem. Eng.">152</a>-<a href="#smll202310426-bib-0157" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0157_R_d140478325e3058" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 157 - Electrochim. Acta">157</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Because of its low cost,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0158" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0158_R_d140478325e3064" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 158 - Chem. Commun.">158</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> high abundance and friendly environment,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0159" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0159_R_d140478325e3069" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 159 - J. Energy Chem.">159</a>, <a href="#smll202310426-bib-0160" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0160_R_d140478325e3069" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 160 - Environ., Development Sustainability">160</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Fe is widely used in research. The Fe<sub>2</sub>P@C electrode synthesized by Qiu et&nbsp;al. has excellent long-term cycling performance when the current density is 3&nbsp;mA&nbsp;cm<sup>−2</sup>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0089" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0089_R_d140478325e3079" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 89 - Chem. Eng. J.">89</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> <b>Figure</b> <a href="#smll202310426-fig-0006">6a–c</a> shows the 3D diagram of Fe<sub>2</sub>P@C anode in situ Raman mode, the superposition diagram of Fe<sub>2</sub>P@C electrode in situ Raman spectrum amplification, and the corresponding constant-current charge-discharge curve, respectively. After 1400 cycles, the Fe<sub>2</sub>P@C electrode still had a high reversible capacity of 0.40&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;cm<sup>−2</sup> with a capacity retention rate of 80.25%, showing excellent cyclic stability. After several cycles, the coulomb efficiency is close to 100%, indicating that Fe<sub>2</sub>P@C electrode has good high current and long-term stability. Fe<sub>2</sub>P@C nanowire aggregation may be caused by internal stress. However, the core-shell structure provides rigidity, effectively preventing agglomeration and ensuring structural integrity. As a result, the volume expansion is significantly reduced, resulting in improved cycle performance. The enhanced stability and cyclic stability achieved by core-shell design fully reflect the advantages of this structure. The 3D foam and nanowire arrays provide a larger contact area for electrolyte penetration, a fast channel for Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion, and a higher density of active materials. Due to the excellent structure of the electrode, the charge transfer resistance is effectively reduced. Zhao et&nbsp;al. synthesized a layered TMP-C hybrid structure consisting of carbon coated with TMP nanoparticles embedded in P and N double-doped porous carbon nanosheets by a simple and scalable one-pot method and carbonization treatment.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0161" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0161_R_d140478325e3106" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 161 - ChemElectroChem">161</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Due to the double carbon protection, P and N double-doped and layered structure, the anode material shows extraordinary sodium ion storage properties. FeP@C shows a significant reversible capacity of 127.8&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 4000 cycles at a high current density of 5.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, with a capacity retention rate of 70.8%. Gao et&nbsp;al. first proposed a self-supported Fe<sub>2</sub>P stacked microsphere array doped with Se (Fe<sub>2</sub>P<sub>0.8</sub>Se<sub>0.2</sub>) to optimize the performance of transition metal phosphide.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0162" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0162_R_d140478325e3124" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 162 - J. Alloys Compd.">162</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> As expected, the Se-doped Fe<sub>2</sub>P array performs significantly better than bare Fe<sub>2</sub>P, providing a highly reversible capacity of 312.5&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 2000&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> and maintaining a capacity of 395.1&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 1000&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 1000 cycles. Most importantly, a uniformly layered array of microspheres tightly anchored to Ni foam can greatly accelerate material transport while maintaining the overall structure even in the case of rapid sodiation/desodiation. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202310426-fig-0006">6d</a> shows the optimization results of Na adsorption on Se-doped Fe<sub>2</sub>P crystals. The adsorption energy (AE) of Na on Se-doped Fe<sub>2</sub>P is calculated to be −3.27&nbsp;eV. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202310426-fig-0006">6e</a> constructs Na diffusion paths in Se-doped Fe<sub>2</sub>P crystals. Combined with the experimental and depth DFT results, it can be concluded that Se doping can regulate the charge density distribution to a large extent, enhance the adsorption capacity of Na, minimize the diffusion energy barrier of Na<sup>+</sup>, increase the active site of sodium conversion, increase the conductivity, and expand the lattice spacing, thereby improving the capacity and cycle stability.</p>
               
               <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
                  <figure class="figure" id="smll202310426-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/92df9790-0ad5-49a6-86bc-5933ebf40028/smll202310426-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                           <source srcset="/cms/asset/92df9790-0ad5-49a6-86bc-5933ebf40028/smll202310426-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/6dc4ec7f-969e-40f2-b091-b8c9228a569b/smll202310426-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/92df9790-0ad5-49a6-86bc-5933ebf40028/smll202310426-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">

Reproduced with permission.<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0089" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0089_R_d140478325e3186" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 89 - Chem. Reproduced with permission.<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0089" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0089_R_d140478325e3192" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 89 - Chem. Reproduced with permission.<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0162" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0162_R_d140478325e3199" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 162 - J. Reproduced with permission.<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0162" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0162_R_d140478325e3207" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 162 - J. Alloys Compd.">162</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Copyright 2022, Elsevier. f) TEM mages of FeP<sub>4</sub>@C-40. Reproduced with permission.<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0127" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0127_R_d140478325e3214" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 127 - J. Alloys Compd.">127</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Copyright 2022, Elsevier. g) Schematic illustrations for the (de)sodiation process of FeP@PNC electrode. Reproduced with permission.<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0126" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0126_R_d140478325e3220" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 126 - Chem. Eng. J.">126</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Copyright 2022, Elsevier.</div>
                     </figcaption>
                  </figure>
               </section>
               <p>Wang et&nbsp;al. synthesized 3D conductive films FeP<sub>4</sub>@C-40 by a simple electrospinning technique combined with phosphorization strategies.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0127" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0127_R_d140478325e3230" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 127 - J. Alloys Compd.">127</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> FeP<sub>4</sub>@C-40 has a unique yolk–shell structure (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202310426-fig-0006">6f</a>). The complete yolk–shell structure helps to reduce the volume expansion of the active substance during the sodium ion insertion process and protects the structure of the composite material from damage, thus effectively improving the long-term cycle performance. And polyacrylonitrile-derived CNFs limit the growth of FeP<sub>4</sub> nanoparticles, which can effectively buffer the volume expansion of FeP<sub>4</sub> during the cycle. The synergistic effect between the unique yolk–shell structural unit and the conductive network of carbon nanofiber makes FeP<sub>4</sub>@C-40 composite have excellent sodium storage properties. Jiang et&nbsp;al. used a one-step method to embed FeP nanoparticles uniformly into a cellular carbon matrix co-doped with N and P.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0126" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0126_R_d140478325e3247" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 126 - Chem. Eng. J.">126</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> This interesting 3D carbon frame structure not only provides additional space for volume expansion during repeated cycles, accordingly improves electrochemical performance, but also provides conductive paths and fast diffusion channels for electrons/ions. The (de)sodiation process of FeP@PNC electrode is shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202310426-fig-0006">6g</a>. The in situ introduction of FeP nanoparticles into vacant carbon through N and P co-doping can significantly reduce the fracture risk after deep cycling and generate more Na ion storage defects at the interface. Due to this novel structure, the FeP@PNC electrode exhibits superior reversibility (340.1&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>), and excellent rate capability of 84.1&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 3&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. It extends cycle life of more than 4500 cycles at 0.5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> without significant capacity decay. In addition, the calculation of the DFT principle shows that there is coupling between FeP and N and P co-doped carbon, which is not only beneficial to charge transfer and strong binding affinity for sodium, but also improves the electrical conductivity of FeP@PNC electrode. The specific capacities of the layered porous FeP@C/rGO nanocomposites synthesized by Wang et&nbsp;al. are 635.7 and 343.1&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 20 and 2000&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0163" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0163_R_d140478325e3271" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 163 - Nanoscale">163</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The cycle is stable. The capacity retention rate is 88.2% after 1000 cycles. Its capacitive contribution is up to 93.9% (2&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>). This reasonably designed FeP@C/rGO layered porous nanostructure achieves a very small volume expansion of only 54.9%, which is much smaller than most conversion anodes. Kinetics and kinetic analysis show that the unique nanostructure design and the synergistic effect between FeP, porous in situ carbon coating, and conductive buffer rGO enable FeP to have a large capacitance contribution behavior and a small volume expansion, resulting in a stable long cycle performance. Shi et&nbsp;al. reasonably designed a novel structure FeP@OCF to confine FeP quantum dots to P-doped 3D octahedral carbon frames/carbon nanotubes.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0164" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0164_R_d140478325e3278" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 164 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">164</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The material has a reversible capacity of 674&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. At 20&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, the high rate performance of 262&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> is still maintained.</p>
               </section>
            
            <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202310426-sec-0120">
               
               <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section3" id="smll202310426-sec-0120-title">4.1.3 V-P</h4>
               
               <p>Kaushik et&nbsp;al. synthesized VP<sub>2</sub> of polycrystals by HEBM.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0087" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0087_R_d140478325e3303" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 87 - J. Power Sources">87</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> <b>Figure</b> <a href="#smll202310426-fig-0007">7a</a> shows the Na storage mechanism diagram of VP<sub>2</sub>. Using ionic liquid as an electrolyte, the initial discharge capacity at 90&nbsp;°C is 243&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. The cycling performance of the VP<sub>2</sub> electrode is then followed by 500 cycles at a current density of 500&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> and temperatures of 25 and 90&nbsp;°C. At 90&nbsp;°C, a high capacity retention rate of 102.4% and a coulomb efficiency of 99.92% are obtained at the 500th cycle compared to the fourth cycle (discharge capacity of 207&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>). The characterization test shows that the interface resistance of Na/VP<sub>2</sub> half cell also gradually decreases with the cycle at 90&nbsp;°C, indicating that a uniform and thin SEI is formed. Due to the large volume expansion and the severe specific capacity reduction of VP<sub>2</sub>, coupling it with conductive carbon-based materials can further improve the electronic conductivity and the stability of composite electrodes and mitigate the huge volume expansion. Ye et&nbsp;al. synthesized VP<sub>2</sub>/3P/C composite with high specific capacity,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0165" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0165_R_d140478325e3332" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 165 - New J. Chem.">165</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> which can reach 550&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 50&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. Even at high temperatures of 60&nbsp;°C, VP<sub>2</sub>/3P/C composite exhibits high capacities of 630 and 375&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 50&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> and 5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. The electrochemical reaction kinetics of VP<sub>2</sub> is regulated by the phosphorus-carbon covalent bond (P─C), which improves its sodium storage performance.</p>
               
               <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
                  <figure class="figure" id="smll202310426-fig-0007"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/3bd094f3-b652-489e-b151-51770b2ed88e/smll202310426-fig-0007-m.jpg"><picture>
                           <source srcset="/cms/asset/3bd094f3-b652-489e-b151-51770b2ed88e/smll202310426-fig-0007-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/c96e4ce4-1f0c-4a78-bf6d-94cabb201158/smll202310426-fig-0007-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/3bd094f3-b652-489e-b151-51770b2ed88e/smll202310426-fig-0007-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                        <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 7<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=smll202310426-fig-0007&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fsmll.202310426" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                        </div>
                        <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) Schematic representation of the conversion reaction mechanism of VP<sub>2</sub>. Reproduced with permission.<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0087" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0087_R_d140478325e3374" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 87 - J. Power Sources">87</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Copyright 2021, Elsevier. b) TEM image of Cu<sub>3</sub>P. Reproduced with permission.<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0128" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0128_R_d140478325e3381" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 128 - Rare Met.">128</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Copyright 2021, Springer Nature. c) Schematic illustration of the mechanism for preparation of Cu<sub>3</sub>P/N-CN composite. Reproduced with permission.<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0129" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0129_R_d140478325e3389" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 129 - J. Alloys Compd.">129</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Copyright 2020, Elsevier.</div>
                     </figcaption>
                  </figure>
               </section>
            </section>
            
            <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202310426-sec-0130">
               
               <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section3" id="smll202310426-sec-0130-title">4.1.4 Cu-P</h4>
               
               <p>According to the Cu-P phase diagram,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0166" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0166_R_d140478325e3403" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 166 - Chem. Rev.">166</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> copper can form three phosphorus compounds Cu<sub>3</sub>P, CuP<sub>2</sub>, and Cu<sub>2</sub>P<sub>7</sub>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0167" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0167_R_d140478325e3417" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 167 - Nano Lett.">167</a>-<a href="#smll202310426-bib-0169" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0169_R_d140478325e3417" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 169 - J. Mater. Chem. A">169</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Among them, Cu<sub>3</sub>P is the most studied anode material due to its air stability. The hollow Cu<sub>3</sub>P anode material (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202310426-fig-0007">7b</a>) synthesized by Zhang et&nbsp;al. has an initial sodium extraction capacity of 159.0&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0128" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0128_R_d140478325e3432" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 128 - Rare Met.">128</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> At 0.2&nbsp;C rate, the capacity retention rate is as high as 85.1% after 50 cycles. And when the current density is increased from 0.2&nbsp;C to 1.6&nbsp;C, 70% of the capacity can be maintained. Cu<sub>3</sub>P is usually compounded with carbonaceous materials to improve the cyclic performance of Cu<sub>3</sub>P. Using NaCl crystals as a template, Xu et&nbsp;al. prepared a 3D porous carbon network (Cu<sub>3</sub>P/N-CN) with nanometer Cu<sub>3</sub>P uniformly embedded in nitrogen doping through a simple and novel freeze-drying strategy.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0129" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0129_R_d140478325e3446" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 129 - J. Alloys Compd.">129</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The preparation process is shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202310426-fig-0007">7c</a>. Cu<sub>3</sub>P nanoparticles can effectively alleviate the physical stress generated during charging and discharging and improve the utilization rate of active materials. Introducing nitrogen through the doping process serves to augment the number of active sites available for sodium storage, concurrently enhancing the electrical conductivity within the carbon network. This strategic infusion of nitrogen not only amplifies the efficacy of sodium ion accommodation but also contributes to an optimized electron transport mechanism within the carbon matrix. The resultant improvement in electrical conductivity translates into accelerated charge and discharge kinetics, thereby fortifying the overall performance of the energy storage system. Furthermore, novel pore structure plays a pivotal role in mitigating the volume expansion experienced by Cu<sub>3</sub>P nanoparticles during the electrochemical processes. At the same time, this structural reinforcement effectively curtails the agglomeration of nanoparticles. With these enhancements, the electrode's structural integrity is reliably maintained, ensuring a sustained and robust performance throughout repeated cycling. In addition, the 3D porous structure enhances the electrical conductivity of Cu<sub>3</sub>P nanoparticles and promotes the rapid diffusion of electrons/ions. Cu<sub>3</sub>P/N-CN(10) showed good cyclic stability. Cu<sub>3</sub>P/N-CN(10) still maintains 340.9&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> discharge capacity at the 100th cycle. And coulomb efficiency remains above 97%. Yin et&nbsp;al. successfully synthesized P/N co-doped carbon nanosheets coated with Cu<sub>3</sub>P nanoparticles (Cu<sub>3</sub>P@P/N-C) using sodium alginate as the biomass carbon source through a feasible aqueous reaction and phosphorization process.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0130" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0130_R_d140478325e3472" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 130 - Front. Chem.">130</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The reasonably designed structure not only improves the ion/electron transfer kinetics but also buffers the volume expansion of Cu<sub>3</sub>P nanoparticles during continuous charging and discharging. In addition, 2D P/N co-doped carbon nanosheets can also serve as conductive substrates, enhancing the electronic conductivity of the entire electrode and providing channels for the rapid diffusion of electrons/ions. Therefore, as anode material for SIBs, it has remarkable cycle stability and rate performance. Notably, Cu<sub>3</sub>P@P/N-C shows an excellent reversible capacity of 209.3&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 1000 cycles. In addition, even at a high current density of 5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, it still maintains the superior specific capacity of 118.2&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 2000 cycles.</p>
               </section>
            
            <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202310426-sec-0140">
               
               <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section3" id="smll202310426-sec-0140-title">4.1.5 Ni-P</h4>
               
               <p>Due to the abundance of phase diagrams, nickel phosphide, such as NiP<sub>2</sub>, Ni<sub>2</sub>P, and Ni<sub>5</sub>P<sub>4</sub>, is the most studied anode material in metal phosphide.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0170" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0170_R_d140478325e3508" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 170 - Inorg. Chem.">170</a>-<a href="#smll202310426-bib-0175" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0175_R_d140478325e3508" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 175 - J. Colloid Interface Sci.">175</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Nickel phosphide can be divided into two categories: phosphorous-rich phase and gold-rich phase. Compared with phosphorous-rich compounds, gold-rich genera such as Ni<sub>2</sub>P and Ni<sub>5</sub>P<sub>4</sub> can be obtained at relatively low temperatures and simpler conditions. In addition, due to their high Ni─Ni bond ratio, they exhibit strong metallic properties and relatively stable cyclability. Zheng et&nbsp;al. synthesized 3D-layered Ni<sub>5</sub>P<sub>4</sub> nanospheres coated with reduced graphene oxide (rGO) nanostructures Ni<sub>5</sub>P<sub>4</sub>@rGO.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0085" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0085_R_d140478325e3529" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 85 - J. Mater. Sci.">85</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> <b>Figure</b> <a href="#smll202310426-fig-0008">8a</a> shows the long-term cyclic performance of the electrode. At 0.2&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, Ni<sub>5</sub>P<sub>4</sub>@rGO can still maintain a high capacity of 304&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 200 cycles, much higher than Ni<sub>5</sub>P<sub>4</sub>. Obviously, the electrochemical properties of Ni<sub>5</sub>P<sub>4</sub>@rGO are greatly improved after reduced graphene oxide (rGO) coating. The excellent electrochemical properties of Ni<sub>5</sub>P<sub>4</sub>@rGO nanocomposite may be attributed to the following three aspects. The encapsulation of Ni<sub>5</sub>P<sub>4</sub> with rGO serves a dual purpose in enhancing the performance of the electrode material. First, this encapsulation process plays a pivotal role in preserving the inherently spherical morphology of Ni<sub>5</sub>P<sub>4</sub> throughout the phosphorization process. By forming a protective layer of reduced graphene oxide around the Ni<sub>5</sub>P<sub>4</sub> particles, this encapsulation effectively prevents them from changing their structure, ensuring that the spherical shape is maintained. In addition to its role in maintaining the morphology of Ni<sub>5</sub>P<sub>4</sub>, rGO assumes a crucial function as a cage-like framework surrounding the entire electrode structure. This 3D framework acts as a formidable barrier, effectively impeding the aggregation and accumulation of active materials during the cyclic charge and discharge processes. By restricting the undue accumulation of active materials, the encapsulation with rGO mitigates the volume change of the electrode material, contributing significantly to the improvement of overall cycle stability. At the same time, the electrical conductivity of rGO can accelerate the Na<sup>+</sup> transfer and reaction kinetics. In addition to designing nickel phosphide as nanostructures, it is often compounded with carbonaceous materials. Liang et&nbsp;al. used metal hydroxide and glucose as precursors to convert metal hydroxide into phosphide in a plasma environment, while glucose was simultaneously decomposed and a carbon shell was formed on the phosphide particles.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0132" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0132_R_d140478325e3582" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 132 - Nano Res.">132</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In this way, the core-shell structure Ni<sub>2</sub>P@C is formed. In situ carbon shell protects Ni<sub>2</sub>P from oxidation. In addition, the high-energy plasma introduces pores and vacancies in Ni<sub>2</sub>P. More importantly, phosphorus-rich nickel phosphide (NiP<sub><i>x</i></sub>) is produced. As a result, the Ni<sub>2</sub>P@C electrode has a high sodium capacity (693&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 50 cycles at 100&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>) and excellent cyclability (maintaining a stable capacity for at least 1500 cycles). Researchers have reported a generalized metal–organic framework derivatization route for the synthesis of layered carbon-encased yolk–shell nickel spheres as anode materials for SIBs.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0176" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0176_R_d140478325e3603" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 176 - J. Colloid Interface Sci.">176</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The nickel metal–organic framework (Ni-MOF) precursor is converted in situ to lamellar carbon-coated Ni<sub>2</sub>P by phosphorization and retains its yolk shell spherical shape. The synthesized Ni<sub>2</sub>P/C sample has a lower polarization and discharge platform, smaller voltage gap, and faster kinetics, resulting in higher initial specific capacity (3222.1/1979.3&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>) and reversible capacity of 765.4&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 110 cycles.</p>
               
               <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
                  <figure class="figure" id="smll202310426-fig-0008"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/e980f692-6d45-4e1d-8762-3cbefbe2933d/smll202310426-fig-0008-m.jpg"><picture>
                           <source srcset="/cms/asset/e980f692-6d45-4e1d-8762-3cbefbe2933d/smll202310426-fig-0008-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/3ccdab17-ddff-4dc1-baf8-38ebfbe07b1c/smll202310426-fig-0008-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/e980f692-6d45-4e1d-8762-3cbefbe2933d/smll202310426-fig-0008-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                        <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 8<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=smll202310426-fig-0008&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fsmll.202310426" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                        </div>
                        <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) Cycling performance of Ni<sub>5</sub>P<sub>4</sub>@rGO at 0.2&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. Reproduced with permission.<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0085" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0085_R_d140478325e3643" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 85 - J. Mater. Sci.">85</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Copyright 2020, Springer Nature. b) Schematic illustration of the morphology and microstructure advantages of the F-NiP<sub>2</sub>@C nanosheets anode. Reproduced with permission.<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0134" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0134_R_d140478325e3651" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 134 - Nano Res.">134</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Copyright 2021, Springer Nature. c) Cycling performances of the NiP<sub>1.5</sub>S<sub>0.5</sub> electrode at 500&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> with initial three cycles at 50&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. Reproduced with permission.<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0131" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0131_R_d140478325e3665" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 131 - Chem. Eng. J.">131</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Copyright 2023, Elsevier. d) HRTEM image of NiP<sub>2</sub>/C nanocomposite. Reproduced with permission.<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0133" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0133_R_d140478325e3672" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 133 - Electrochim. Acta">133</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Copyright 2022, Elsevier. e) Rate capacity from 0.5 to 5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> of HMN MoP@C as anode for SIBs. Reproduced with permission.<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0179" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0179_R_d140478325e3680" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 179 - Electrochim. Acta">179</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Copyright 2021, Elsevier. f) Schematic illustration of the synthetic process of MoP@NCNF. Reproduced with permission.<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0135" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0135_R_d140478325e3685" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 135 - Electrochim. Acta">135</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Copyright 2020, Elsevier.</div>
                     </figcaption>
                  </figure>
               </section>
               <p>The phosphorus-rich phase NiP<sub>2</sub> has a high theoretical capacity and is expected to be used in SIBs anodes. Wu et&nbsp;al. successfully modulated the electronic structure of NiP<sub>2</sub> by heteroatom (F) doping and the introduction of vacancy defects to enhance the adsorption site and diffusion kinetics of Na<sup>+</sup>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0134" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0134_R_d140478325e3699" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 134 - Nano Res.">134</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The distinctive 3D carbonaceous network structure effectively enhances the electronic conductivity of the electrode, facilitating rapid charge transfer kinetics of the NiP<sub>2</sub> active material and reducing the diffusion length of Na<sup>+</sup>. Second, compared to a single carbon matrix, the 3D bicontinuous carbon matrix efficiently confines NiP<sub>2</sub> particles and mitigates the substantial volume changes during the repeated sodiation/desodiation process, ensuring superior cycle stability of NiP<sub>2</sub> particles. The synthesized 3D bicontinous carbon matrix is decorated with well-dispersed fluorine (F) doped NiP<sub>2</sub> nanoparticles (F-NiP<sub>2</sub>@C nanosheets), which possesses high reversible capacity of 585&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> and excellent long cycle stability of 244&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> over 1000 cycles at 2&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. Density functional theory (DFT) calculation shows that doping F in NiP<sub>2</sub> can induce the formation of P vacancy, increase the adsorption energy of Na<sup>+</sup>, and accelerate the alloying of P components. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202310426-fig-0008">8b</a> shows the morphology and microstructure of F-NiP<sub>2</sub>@C nanosheets. Kim et&nbsp;al. prepared solid solution series by high-energy mechanical milling and studied their electrochemical properties as anode material of SIBs.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0131" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0131_R_d140478325e3736" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 131 - Chem. Eng. J.">131</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> A complete solid solution is achieved between the two end members (NiP<sub>2</sub> and NiS<sub>2</sub>). The synthesized NiP<sub>2</sub>-xS<sub><i>x</i></sub> solid solution is nano-powder with a size of several hundred nanometers composed of nanocrystals with a size of ≈20&nbsp;nm. The solid solution affects the redox reaction of each end element, changes the sodiation/desodiation potentials, activates the reaction between P and Na<sup>+</sup>, and increases the discharge capacity. NiP<sub>2</sub>-xS<sub><i>x</i></sub> solid solution and Na<sup>+</sup> undergo a sequential conversion reaction to form nano-composite sodium products (Na<sub>3</sub>P, Na<sub>2</sub>S, and Ni), which effectively reduces the volume change, prevents the agglomeration of active materials and ensures the transfer of electrons and ions. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202310426-fig-0008">8c</a>, the NiP<sub>1.5</sub>S<sub>0.5</sub> solid solution electrode exhibits excellent cyclic stability, providing a reversible capacity of 299&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 200 cycles at a high current density of 500&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. Lee et&nbsp;al. prepared NiP<sub>2</sub>/C nanocomposites using synthetic NiP<sub>2</sub> and acetylene carbon black as raw materials by high-energy mechanical milling (HEMM).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0133" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0133_R_d140478325e3781" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 133 - Electrochim. Acta">133</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> A high-resolution transmission electron microscopy (HRTEM) image (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202310426-fig-0008">8d</a>) shows that nano NiP<sub>2</sub> is completely covered with a carbon layer ≈10&nbsp;nm thick. At a current density of 50&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, the specific capacity of the NiP<sub>2</sub>/C nanocomposite reaches 428&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 100 cycles. The high conductivity, high mobility of Na<sup>+</sup> ions, and the decrease of nanoparticle aggregation during the cycling of NiP<sub>2</sub>/C nanocomposite are the main reasons for the enhancement of the cycling performance. In addition, NiP<sub>2</sub>/C nanocomposite operates successfully even in a full battery configuration.</p>
               </section>
            
            <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202310426-sec-0150">
               
               <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section3" id="smll202310426-sec-0150-title">4.1.6 Mo-P</h4>
               
               <p>Molybdenum phosphide has also recently been used in the anode of SIBs.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0177" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0177_R_d140478325e3814" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 177 - New J. Chem.">177</a>, <a href="#smll202310426-bib-0178" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0178_R_d140478325e3814" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 178 - Adv. Energy Mater.">178</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Zhao et&nbsp;al. designed a simple chelating, carbonizing, and package phosphating process to construct MoP@C composite.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0179" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0179_R_d140478325e3819" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 179 - Electrochim. Acta">179</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The ultra-small MoP nanocrystal with a diameter of 5–6&nbsp;nm are tightly and uniformly embedded into ultra-thin amorphous carbon nanosheets with a thickness of ≈10&nbsp;nm, and then further assembled into layered mesoporous nanospheres with abundant mesoporous and large surface area (90.1&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>). The multiple structural advantages significantly improve the electrochemical activity, electronic conductivity, and structural stability of MoP and lead to superior sodium ion storage performance. It has a reversible capacity of up to 770&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> current density. The cyclic stability is excellent. At 1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> current density, the discharge capacity after 400 cycles is 464&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202310426-fig-0008">8e</a>, MoP@C has excellent rate properties. At 5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> current density, the average discharge capacity is 264&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. Fu et&nbsp;al. prepared high-performance MoP@N doped carbon nanofiber anode (MoP@NCNFs) by electrospinning and in situ carbothermal auto-reduction process.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0135" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0135_R_d140478325e3845" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 135 - Electrochim. Acta">135</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The synthesis process is shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202310426-fig-0008">8f</a>. The well-crystallized MoP nanoparticles are evenly distributed in the interwoven nanofibers, providing a conductive network for rapid charge/ion transport. Benefiting from gas activation during carbonization, layered pores are formed in the nanofibers. This unique structure should be able to provide sufficient buffer space for volume expansion in the conversion reaction and promote the rapid transport of electrolytes. The cycle performance is well improved. At 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, MoP@NCNFs have an initial discharge and charge capacity of 1029 and 586&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively, within the voltage window of 0.01–3.0&nbsp;V (vs Na/Na<sup>+</sup>). After the initial cycle capacity declines, the steady–state cycle is gradually realized. After 200 cycles, the reversible specific capacity remains 376&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. At 2&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> and 100% CE, the reversible capacity of 117&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> can be maintained after 1000 cycles.</p>
               </section>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202310426-sec-0160">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="smll202310426-sec-0160-title">4.2 Converted-Alloyed Metal Phosphides for Sodium Storage</h3>
            
            <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202310426-sec-0170">
               
               <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section3" id="smll202310426-sec-0170-title">4.2.1 Ge-P</h4>
               
               <p>In addition to the above materials, germanium phosphide has been developed for the anode of SIBs.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0180" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0180_R_d140478325e3881" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 180 - J. Power Sources">180</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> By combining conductive base materials or excellent nanostructures, the samples exhibit excellent electrochemical properties. Wang et&nbsp;al. prepared GeP<sub>3</sub>/C@rGO by HEBM.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0137" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0137_R_d140478325e3888" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 137 - ACS Nano">137</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In the process of HEBM, the strong P─O─C chemical bond interaction between GeP<sub>3</sub> and the carbon matrix is also conducive to the stability of the electrode material, so that it has a high reversible capacity during the cycle. The addition of carbon matrix and graphene oxide nanosheets with strain buffering effect can effectively inhibit the volume expansion of electrode material, thus improving the cyclic stability of electrode materials. The material has a reversible high capacity of 1084&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 50&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. It has an excellent rate capacity of 435.4&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. It has long-term cyclic stability. The reversible capacity remains 823.3&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.2&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 400 cycles. Based on in situ X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy and in situ electrochemical impedance spectroscopy, the carbon matrix acts to activate and stabilize the interior of the composite, while the graphene acts to protect and inhibit the exterior surface of the composite. <b>Figure</b> <a href="#smll202310426-fig-0009">9a</a> shows the electrode cycle diagram of the material. Because of the synergistic combination of these two components, GeP<sub>3</sub>/C@rGO achieves extremely stable cycle stability and excellent rate performance. Zeng et&nbsp;al. prepared a hollow nanoreactor with a unique structure using a simple electrospinning method and sealed phosphorization process and assembled them with a conductive nitrogen-doped carbon network for in situ synthesis of GeP/CN electrode.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0078" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0078_R_d140478325e3917" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 78 - Angew. Chem.">78</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The self-supported electrode has rich porosity, high conductivity, and excellent mechanical stability, which can not only be used as a container to control the growth of GeP crystal in the phosphating process but also effectively inhibit the volume change of GeP during the sodiation/desodiation process. By changing the fiber width, hollow size, and tube thickness, the confinement effect and Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics of the nanoreactor can be ideally adjusted. The reversible capacity of the optimized GeP/CN-3 electrode at 100 and 4000&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> is 830 and 330&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. It also has excellent cycle stability over 350 cycles at 500&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>.</p>
               
               <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
                  <figure class="figure" id="smll202310426-fig-0009"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/6ab2c6c7-9e4a-4247-9829-ac0905327893/smll202310426-fig-0009-m.jpg"><picture>
                           <source srcset="/cms/asset/6ab2c6c7-9e4a-4247-9829-ac0905327893/smll202310426-fig-0009-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/7dd7dae9-e32d-4c37-a897-b2037b488c3a/smll202310426-fig-0009-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/6ab2c6c7-9e4a-4247-9829-ac0905327893/smll202310426-fig-0009-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                        <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 9<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=smll202310426-fig-0009&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fsmll.202310426" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                        </div>
                        <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) GeP<sub>3</sub>/C@rGO electrodes during cycles. Reproduced with permission.<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0137" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0137_R_d140478325e3953" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 137 - ACS Nano">137</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Copyright 2020, American Chemical Society. b) Schematic of the mechanism of the sodiation and desodiation in Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>/GT anode. Reproduced with permission.<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0181" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0181_R_d140478325e3963" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 181 - Adv. Energy Mater.">181</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Copyright 2021, John Wiley and Sons. c) Schematic illustration of the Na<sup>+</sup> storage mechanism and electronic conductivity in the Sn/Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>@MXene-2 nanocomposite. Reproduced with permission.<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0182" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0182_R_d140478325e3975" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 182 - J. Power Sources">182</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Copyright 2023, Elsevier. d) CV profile of the capacitive contribution at 0.8&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup> for Sn<sub><i>x</i></sub>P<sub>y</sub>/NG electrode. Reproduced with permission.<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0113" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0113_R_d140478325e3987" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 113 - J. Alloys Compd.">113</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Copyright 2023, Elsevier. e) Cycling performance of Sn/P@G, Sn/P@CNTs, and Sn/P@G-CNTs composites at 100&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. Reproduced with permission.<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0088" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0088_R_d140478325e3995" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 88 - Electrochim. Acta">88</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Copyright 2021, Elsevier.</div>
                     </figcaption>
                  </figure>
               </section>
            </section>
            
            <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202310426-sec-0180">
               
               <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section3" id="smll202310426-sec-0180-title">4.2.2 Sn-P</h4>
               
               <p>As the SIBs anode material, Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> has received particular attention due to its high theoretical capacity (1132&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>),<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0084" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0084_R_d140478325e4015" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 84 - Nano Lett.">84</a>, <a href="#smll202310426-bib-0183" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0183_R_d140478325e4015" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 183 - J. Power Sources">183</a>-<a href="#smll202310426-bib-0187" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0187_R_d140478325e4015" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 187 - Appl. Surf. Sci.">187</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> high theoretical volume-specific capacity (6650&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;cm<sup>−3</sup>),<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0107" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0107_R_d140478325e4023" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 107 - Adv. Energy Mater.">107</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> high electrical conductivity (30.7&nbsp;S&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup>), and low redox potential (0.3&nbsp;V vs Na/Na<sup>+</sup>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0076" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0076_R_d140478325e4033" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 76 - Adv. Mater.">76</a>, <a href="#smll202310426-bib-0107" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0107_R_d140478325e4033" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 107 - Adv. Energy Mater.">107</a>, <a href="#smll202310426-bib-0188" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0188_R_d140478325e4033" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 188 - J. Mater. Chem. A">188</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Tan et&nbsp;al. synthesized Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>/GT by restricting the growth of Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> nanoparticles in amphiphilic graphene tubes.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0181" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0181_R_d140478325e4047" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 181 - Adv. Energy Mater.">181</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> This method provides mechanical robustness, the ability to confine Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> particles through its highly conductive framework, and the ability to adapt the particles' volume changes during the cycle. This unique structure gives the anode material a high reversible capacity (821&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>), excellent rate capacity (326&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 20&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>), and cyclic stability (90% reversible capacity maintained after 500 cycles). This strategy can be extended to other conversion-alloy-type materials that experience large volume changes during charge and discharge. The sodiation and desodiation mechanism of the material is shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202310426-fig-0009">9b</a>. Fan et&nbsp;al. added Sn and Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> nanoparticles between MXene sheets. The method converts 2D MXene into a 3D conductive network.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0182" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0182_R_d140478325e4070" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 182 - J. Power Sources">182</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The uniform distribution of the ultra-small Sn nanoparticles (≈4&nbsp;nm in diameter) ensures high conductivity. It is not only along but also perpendicular to the MXene plane. And the covalent Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> nanoparticles significantly enhance their structural stability. The Sn and Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> nanoparticles act as pillars to prevent the accumulation of MXene sheets. Good specific surface area and stratified pore characteristics can reduce the structural strain during the electrochemical reaction and stimulate electrolyte penetration, significantly improving cycling performance. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202310426-fig-0009">9c</a> shows the storage mechanism and electronic conductivity of Na<sup>+</sup> in Sn/Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>@MXene nanocomposite. In addition, in/ex situ characterization reveals that the Na<sup>+</sup> insertion/extraction process in the network has fairly high reversibility. The 3D conductive network produces enhanced capacity. Sn/Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>@MXene shows excellent electrochemical properties. It also has excellent long-term cycle stability (127.2&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 1000 cycles at 5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>). Some researchers synthesized Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> particles in the CN matrix and utilized the inhibition effects of the carbon matrix to make Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> nanoparticles distribute uniformly on the composite material.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0091" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0091_R_d140478325e4114" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 91 - J. Alloys Compd.">91</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> SIBs with Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>/CN as the anode have excellent capacity performance. It can maintain 476.6&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 60 cycles. The specific capacities of ≈430, ≈310, ≈245, and ≈190&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> can be achieved under 1, 1.5, 2, and 3&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. The dispersed arrangement of nano Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> particles within the carbon matrix contributes to an interconnected network that promotes efficient charge transfer, ultimately improving the overall electronic conductivity of the composite material. By preventing the agglomeration of particles, the carbon matrix facilitates a more uniform and stable distribution of stress during cycling, limiting the detrimental effects of volume expansion. These factors collectively contribute to the preservation of stable cycling performance. Zhao et&nbsp;al. synthesized Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>@CNF by electrospinning and phosphorization. They constructed hollow yolk shell Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>@C nanospheres into nano-chain structure, in which all the hollow Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> nanospheres were uniformly linked to 1D carbon nanofibers to form a mixed conductive structure with chain shape.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0189" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0189_R_d140478325e4149" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 189 - Carbon">189</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>@CNF electrode provides a highly reversible discharge capacity of 297.6&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 1750 cycles and 250.6&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 2&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 4700 cycles. The material has stable cycle durability. At a high rate current of 5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, the capacity is still 157.8&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 14&nbsp;000 cycles. Liu et&nbsp;al. proposed an efficient one-step synthesis of Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> nanostructures based on simultaneous reduction and in situ phosphorylation of SnCl<sub>4</sub> and PCl<sub>3</sub> on mechanically activated Na surfaces.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0136" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0136_R_d140478325e4181" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 136 - Nano Res.">136</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In addition, this simple method has a strong control over the size of the phosphide. Ultrafine Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> nanocrystals (&lt;5&nbsp;nm) loaded on carbon sheets (Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>/C) were obtained due to the unique bottom-up surface confinement reaction. The Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>/C electrode provides a fairly stable capacity of ≈590&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> over 50 cycles. At high current densities of 2.0 and 5.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, the specific capacities can reach 500 and 430&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. The Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>/C anode shows a long cycle life at a high current density of 1.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, maintaining a high capacity of 420&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> even after 400 cycles.</p>
               
               <p>The Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub>@CNT/C synthesized by Ran et&nbsp;al. reached 742&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 150 cycles at 0.2&nbsp;C.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0190" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0190_R_d140478325e4223" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 190 - ACS Nano">190</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> After 500 cycles at 2&nbsp;C, the rate performance reaches 449&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. A new nanostructure, the yolk–shell, was also applied by the researchers to improve the cycling performance of tin phosphide. Sn<sub>6</sub>O<sub>4</sub>(OH)<sub>4</sub>/NG was used as a precursor to design and synthesize tin phosphide composite material (Sn<sub><i>x</i></sub>P<sub>y</sub>/NG) with yolk–shell nanostructure by one-step carbonization and phosphorylation.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0113" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0113_R_d140478325e4243" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 113 - J. Alloys Compd.">113</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Sn<sub><i>x</i></sub>P<sub>y</sub>/NG electrodes with yolk–shell nanostructure have better energy storage performance than nanoclusters or nanoparticles. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202310426-fig-0009">9d</a> shows the CV curve of the capacitance contribution of the Sn<sub><i>x</i></sub>P<sub>y</sub>/NG electrode at 0.8&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>. The gaps within the yolk–shell nanostructure serve as expansion zones, allowing the active material to undergo necessary volume changes without compromising the structural integrity of the electrode. As a result, the cycle stability is substantially improved, ensuring a more reliable and enduring performance over multiple charge-discharge cycles. The unique coordination of Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> and SnP<sub>0.94</sub> promotes the reaction kinetics. Thus, Sn<sub><i>x</i></sub>P<sub>y</sub>/NG maintains a capacity of 203.1&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 300 cycles at 1.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. It provides long-term cycle stability at a high rate for SIBs. The Sn/P@G-CNTs electrode synthesized by Zhang et&nbsp;al. using HEBM had a high discharge capacity (1048&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 100&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>) at the 100th cycle.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0088" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0088_R_d140478325e4285" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 88 - Electrochim. Acta">88</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The low initial coulomb efficiency of Sn/P@G-CNTs (≈80%) is due to the formation of the irreversible solid electrolyte interface (SEI) on the active material surface, which mainly occurs in the first cycle and is negligible in subsequent cycles. As can be seen from Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202310426-fig-0009">9e</a>, after 100 cycles at 100&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, the initial capacity retention rate of Sn/P@GCNTS is ≈73% and CE is higher than 98%. The incorporation of G-CNTs into the matrix facilitates the formation of a loose structure for Sn/P@G-CNTs, alleviating the aggregation of Sn/P during the sodiation/desodiation process. Additionally, the introduction of the G-CNTs matrix plays a positive role in reducing volume expansion and enhancing structural stability, thereby endowing the Sn/P@G-CNTs composite material with excellent cyclic stability. This stable cycling performance has the potential for large-scale applications at high current densities. At the same time, it is calculated that the excellent rate performance and cyclic stability of Sn/P@GCNTs are mainly due to the dispersed Sn/P particles and the introduction of the G-CNTs matrix.</p>
               </section>
            
            <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202310426-sec-0190">
               
               <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section3" id="smll202310426-sec-0190-title">4.2.3 Zn-P</h4>
               
               <p>Nam et&nbsp;al. synthesized ZnP<sub>2</sub> by a simple solid-state heat treatment process and then modified ZnP<sub>2</sub>-C composite material by C modification.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0138" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0138_R_d140478325e4308" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 138 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">138</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In the process of sodium conversion, ZnP<sub>2</sub> in the composite is transformed into NaZn<sub>13</sub> and Na<sub>3</sub>P phases, which is a one-step conversion reaction. In contrast, Zn and P in NaZn<sub>13</sub> and Na<sub>3</sub>P are completely recombined into ZnP<sub>2</sub> phases during desodiation, respectively. Due to the one-step conversion/recombination of ZnP<sub>2</sub> in the composite during the cycle, ZnP<sub>2</sub>-C has a highly reversible capacity of 883&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> with no capacity attenuation after 130 cycles. It also has fast rate performance capability of 500 and 350&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 1&nbsp;C and 3&nbsp;C, respectively.</p>
               </section>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202310426-sec-0200">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="smll202310426-sec-0200-title">4.3 Polymetallic Phosphides for Sodium Storage</h3>
            
            <p>Due to the existence of multiple metal sites, the theoretical specific capacity of polymetallic phosphide is further improved.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0171" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0171_R_d140478325e4346" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 171 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">171</a>, <a href="#smll202310426-bib-0191" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0191_R_d140478325e4346" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 191 - ACS Appl. Energy Mater.">191</a>-<a href="#smll202310426-bib-0196" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0196_R_d140478325e4346" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 196 - J. Alloys Compd.">196</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Moreover, the synergistic effect between the elements in polymetallic phosphide is conducive to improving the cycle stability. The bimetallic phosphide Ni<sub>2</sub>P/CoP@rGO heterojunction synthesized by Zhou et&nbsp;al. has an initial discharge capacity of 770.1&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0095" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0095_R_d140478325e4355" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 95 - J. Power Sources">95</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In the second cycle, it decays to 293.5&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, which is due to the formation of the SEI. As shown in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#smll202310426-fig-0010">10a</a>, Ni<sub>2</sub>P/CoP@rGO offers higher rate performance of 436.7, 375.3, 332.7, 290.8, 233.3, and 197.8&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at current densities ranging from 0.02 to 1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. Upon restoration to 0.2&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, the reversible capacity recovers to 272.3&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> and maintains 270.4&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 100 cycles. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202310426-fig-0010">10b</a>, the Ni<sub>2</sub>P/CoP@rGO electrode has a higher reversible capacity of 193.8&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 100 cycles with coulomb efficiency approaching 100%. The Ni<sub>2</sub>P/CoP heterostructure not only creates a built-in electric field but also generates abundant vacancies, synergistically enhancing the diffusion capability of Na<sup>+</sup> and amplifying the number of electrochemical reaction sites. This dynamic interplay of structural features contributes to an optimized electrochemical performance. The incorporation of rGO serves to ameliorate volume expansion concerns, providing mechanical support to the electrode and concurrently elevating the ion and electron transport rates during charge and discharge cycles. Combined with these advantages, Ni<sub>2</sub>P/CoP@rGO exhibits superior rate performance and cycle stability as SIBs anode material.</p>
