                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <div class="paragraph-element">The Zn<sub>0.5</sub>Ge<sub>0.5</sub>P-C composite was prepared by grinding Zn<sub>0.5</sub>Ge<sub>0.5</sub>P and Super P (C) in a mass ratio of 65:35 for 10 h.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0097" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0097_R_d140478325e4474" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 97 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">97</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202310426-fig-0010">10c</a> shows the long-period performance of Zn<sub>0.5</sub>Ge<sub>0.5</sub>P-C under fast charge and discharge. When the current density is 20&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (50&nbsp;°C), the first cycle discharge capacity is 483.5&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, and the charging capacity is 377.8&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. After 500 cycles, it still shows a reverse specific capacity of 339&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, maintaining the capacity of 89.7%. The incorporation of two metal elements in bimetallic phosphide materials endows them with several advantages, including increased phase diversity, a plethora of Na<sup>+</sup> binding sites, abundant pathways for ion migration, stress relief capabilities, enhanced electronic conduction, and synergistic effects. Notably, when compared to monometallic phosphide materials, each element in bimetallic phosphating materials serves a fundamental and unique role in promoting synergies, collectively enhancing the overall performance of the material. The presence of Ge within the structure maintains a robust diamond-like framework, while P contributes a substantial Na<sup>+</sup> storage capacity. The addition of Na-reactive Zn not only mitigates volume changes but also ensures the smooth diffusion of sodium ions. These elements, when combined, play a synergistic role in elevating the electrochemical performance of Zn<sub>0.5</sub>Ge<sub>0.5</sub>P anodes. Furthermore, Zn<sub>0.5</sub>Ge<sub>0.5</sub>P ─C composites feature bonds such as Zn─C, Ge─P, P─C, and P─O─C, which contribute to stress relief mechanisms, preventing material cracking and detachment. The synergistic effects of the diverse elements present in the bimetallic phosphide materials and the carefully engineered composites underscore their potential for advanced energy storage applications with improved cycle stability. The Na<sup>+</sup> storage process of Zn<sub>0.5</sub>Ge<sub>0.5</sub>P is an alloy-type reaction that produces NaP, Na<sub>3</sub>P, NaGe, and NaZn<sub>13</sub> phases, whose uniform distribution guarantees electrochemical reversibility in desodiation process. The reaction process is inferred as Equation&nbsp;(<a class="equationLink scrollableLink" href="#smll202310426-disp-0003" title="Link to equation">3</a>):

               <div class="inline-equation" id="smll202310426-disp-0003"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
                     <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/5958a64e-c687-4343-92bc-1d432822483b/smll202310426-math-0003.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:16136810:media:smll202310426:smll202310426-math-0003" display="block" location="graphic/smll202310426-math-0003.png">

                                    </mrow>

                           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{eqnarray} 2Z{{\mathrm{n}}}_{0.5}{\rm G{e}}_{0.5}{\rm P} &amp;+&amp; \left( {5 + 1/13} \right){\rm Na} \Leftrightarrow {\rm NaP}\nonumber\\ &amp;+&amp; {\rm N{a}}_3P + {\rm NaGe} + 1/13{\rm NaZ{n}}_{13} \end{eqnarray}$$</annotation>
                        </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(3)</span></div>
            </div>
            
            <p>Li et&nbsp;al. have demonstrated a low-cost and simple strategy for the first time.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0197" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0197_R_d140478325e4596" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 197 - J. Mater. Sci. Technol.">197</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> This strategy is used to synthesize Ni, N co-doped graphitized carbon (C) and cobalt phosphide (CoP) embedded carbon fiber (Ni-CoP@C-N⊂CF) as self-supporting anode material. Graphitized carbon and carbon fiber improve electrical conductivity and suppress the volume expansion problem. In addition, the microporous structure and ultra-small size of Ni-CoP provide high surface area for short Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion paths, fast charge transport dynamics, and electrolyte wettability. The results show that the average capacity of the material decreases by 0.04% at 2000&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. At 2000&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, it has an excellent rate performance of 270&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> and a high energy density of 231.1&nbsp;Wh&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup> and has excellent electrochemical properties. Chen et&nbsp;al. prepared a self-supported iron-nickel phosphide (Fe-Ni-P) composite with a nanosheet array through a reasonable hydrothermal reaction and phosphating process.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0092" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0092_R_d140478325e4612" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 92 - J. Electroanal. Chem.">92</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The construction of a nanosheet array can significantly release mechanical strain and promote electrochemical reaction kinetics. In addition, Fe-Ni-P electrodes exhibit better cyclic stability than Fe<sub>2</sub>P and Ni<sub>2</sub>P electrodes, which may be due to the bimetal synergistic effect of effectively inhibiting volume expansion and maintaining good structural stability. Owing to its unique design, the robust Fe-Ni-P array exhibits superior Na<sup>+</sup> storage capability. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202310426-fig-0010">10d–f</a> shows the electrochemical correlation test diagram of the material. The discharge capacity of Fe-Ni-P nanosheet reaches 300.9&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 100 cycles at 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. At the current density of 0.5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, the material can maintain the reversible capacity of 201.7&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 200 cycles, with unobvious capacity loss. The nano-sheet Fe-Ni-P array retains its shape and is tightly attached to the Ni foam. The ideal structural stability of Fe-Ni-P array is an important guarantee for its competitive cycle performance.</p>
            
            <p>The rod-like Cu-Fe-P/TiN synthesized by Zhou et&nbsp;al. can provide a highly reversible capacity of more than 180&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 50&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> and achieve a capacity retention rate of 70% after 100 cycles.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0105" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0105_R_d140478325e4642" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 105 - J. Power Sources">105</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> When the surface current density is 1&nbsp;mA&nbsp;cm<sup>−2</sup>, the reversible capacity of Cu-Fe-P/TiN electrode is 1.6&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;cm<sup>−2</sup>. The electrode cycle process of the material is shown in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#smll202310426-fig-0011">11a</a>. Li et&nbsp;al. synthesized FeP spheres containing copper and carbon in a yolk shell (YS-Cu-FeP@C) by a simple template bonding method.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0139" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0139_R_d140478325e4658" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 139 - Chem. Eng. J.">139</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202310426-fig-0011">11b,c</a> shows the structure model and corresponding charge density distribution of Cu-doped FeP, respectively. Copper is doped into FeP, and an N-doped carbon layer is coated on the surface of yolk–shell FeP sphere. With the help of unique composition and structural advantages, the synthesized YS-Cu-FeP@C sphere has enhanced electrochemical properties of SIBs, including excellent rate capability (145&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 10&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>) and excellent long-term cycle performance (up to 900 cycles at 1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>). Some researchers have reported the synthesis of amorphous Sn<sub>0.5</sub>Ge<sub>0.5</sub>P<sub>3</sub>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0140" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0140_R_d140478325e4680" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 140 - ACS Nano">140</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Through a two-phase transition strategy, the two crystals are adjusted based on the elemental composition and used as the anode material for SIBs. The prepared Sn<sub>0.5</sub>Ge<sub>0.5</sub>P<sub>3</sub> has a reversible sodium storage capacity of 1397&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> and maintains a capacity of 1132&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> over 100 cycles. Even at high current densities of 0.5, 2, and 10&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, the capacities reach 980, 666, and 321&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. The elastic amorphous structure of the electrode reduces the expansion stress and reversibly maintains the integrity of the electrode. In addition, the short-range order of cations and anions in Sn<sub>0.5</sub>Ge<sub>0.5</sub>P<sub>3</sub> effectively inhibits the element separation. And the long-range disorder structure reduces the bond dissociation energy and shortens the ion transport distance, which is conducive to the rapid ion diffusion dynamics. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202310426-fig-0011">11d</a> shows the thickness changes of GeP<sub>3</sub>, Sn<sub>0.5</sub>Ge<sub>0.5</sub>P<sub>3</sub>, and SnP<sub>3</sub> electrodes during the first 10 cycles. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202310426-fig-0011">11e</a> shows the EIS of GeP<sub>3</sub>, Sn<sub>0.5</sub>Ge<sub>0.5</sub>P<sub>3</sub>, and SnP<sub>3</sub> electrodes after 10 cycles. The heterogeneous structure of CoP/FeP coated with a carbon layer and encapsulated within hollow porous carbon balls (HPCBs) was prepared by room-temperature wet chemistry and phosphatization using a Prussian blue analog as a precursor.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0141" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0141_R_d140478325e4737" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 141 - J. Electroanal. Chem.">141</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> And the sphere-in-sphere structure with an internal void was constructed. The outstanding characteristics of the composite can be attributed to the meticulous design of the metal phosphide heterostructure, coupled with the concurrent coating and confinement effects of carbonaceous materials. Experimental and theoretical calculations substantiate the construction of the heterostructure, showcasing its ability to facilitate charge redistribution and lattice distortion, thereby enhancing internal reaction kinetics. Additionally, the incorporation of dual carbonaceous materials, equipped with the capability to prevent the aggregation of active substances, synergizes with the exceptional mechanical buffering provided by interior voids in HPCBs. The superior electrical characteristics of carbon layers and HPCBs further contribute to promoting external energy storage kinetics and facilitating intergranular charge transfer. This research not only offers insights into the effective strategy employed for optimizing internal/external reaction kinetics but also provides a promising approach for cycle stability in SIBs. At 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, the CoFe-P@C@Void@HPCBs electrode can maintain the capacity of 397&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 100 cycles. A novel electrode material Co<sub>0.7</sub>Mo<sub>0.3</sub>P/NC containing bimetallic Co and Mo in a nitrogen-doped carbon base has been proposed.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0142" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0142_R_d140478325e4751" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 142 - J. Power Sources">142</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The electrode has a first discharge/charge capacity of 904/565&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> and maintains a high discharge capacity of 475&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> for the following cycle. After five cycles, good overlapping voltage distribution indicates good cycle stability. The Co<sub>0.7</sub>Mo<sub>0.3</sub>P/NC electrode can still reach a good capacity of 160&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 1000 cycles at 1.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, and the CE is close to 100%. The excellent performance is due to the electronic structure modification and the unique nanostructure of the hybrid composite. The Co<sub>0.7</sub>Mo<sub>0.3</sub>P/NC obtained by adjusting the optimized atomic ratio has excellent rate performance and high cyclic stability. Density functional theory (DFT) calculations show that the improved performance is due to the optimized electronic structure and the rich Fermi energy center density. Li et&nbsp;al. prepared Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub> hollow microspheres using PMMA microspheres as sacrificial templates and grew S-doped NiCoP nanosheets with abundant S vacancy on Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub> surface by a stepwise strategy to obtain the hollow Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>@S-NiCoP.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0143" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0143_R_d140478325e4796" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 143 - J. Mater. Chem. A">143</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> When used as SIBs anode, Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>@S-NiCoP has a reversible capacity of 563&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.2&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. It also provides excellent cycle stability for more than 3000 cycles with a capacity decay of 0.005% per cycle. DFT calculations combined with XPS and XANES tests demonstrate that the excellent electrochemical properties can be attributed to the strong interaction of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>@S-NiCoP at the heterogeneous interface, resulting in improved electrical conductivity and structural integrity. The incorporation of S doping results in an increased abundance of sulfur vacancies, offering a higher number of active sites that facilitate the adsorption and conversion of sodium ions. Furthermore, the hollow structure within the material serves a multifaceted role: first, it alleviates the volume expansion associated with the sodiation/desodiation processes, thereby preserving the structural stability of the electrode material. Second, the hollow architecture accelerates electrolyte penetration, promotes effective ion transport within the material, and improves sodium storage kinetics. The combination of these features collectively leads to a substantial enhancement in the cyclic stability of Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>@S-NiCoP in SIBs. Fe-doped CoP/CM synthesized by Xu et&nbsp;al. was used as the anode material of SIBs with a high specific capacity of 515&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 100&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 100 cycles.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0198" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0198_R_d140478325e4833" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 198 - Chem.–A European J.">198</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Even if the current density rises to 500&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, the specific capacity remains 324&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 500 cycles, showing superior rate performance and cyclability. The porous yolk shell MoP/Cu<sub>3</sub>P@C micro-cage synthesized by Yin et&nbsp;al. has a reversible capacity of 307.8&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 1.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0199" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0199_R_d140478325e4849" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 199 - Energy Environ. Mater.">199</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The excellent cycle stability of 132.1&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> is still achieved after 6000 cycles at 5.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. Han et&nbsp;al. synthesized CoP/FeP@PCNFs by embedding different CoP/FeP nanoparticles in porous carbon nanofibers.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0200" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0200_R_d140478325e4859" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 200 - Nanoscale">200</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The material can achieve a large reversible specific capacity of 459&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.05&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. The volume retention rate at 10&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> is 46.4% (compared to 0.05&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>). The cycle stability is well performed with a capacity of 208&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 1000 cycles. And the capacity retention rate is 73.5%.</p>

         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202310426-sec-0210">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="smll202310426-sec-0210-title">4.4 Electrolyte Additive in SIBs of Metal Phosphide</h3>
            
            <p>In the realm of electrochemical reactions, it must be recognized that the electrolyte system plays a crucial role not only in the volume expansion of metal phosphide anodes but also in the intermediates produced in these reactions.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0201" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0201_R_d140478325e4957" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 201 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">201</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The selection of electrolyte composition, concentration, and overall composition of electrolyte solution have significant effects on the electrochemical performance of metal phosphide anodes. In the charge and discharge cycle, the electrolyte acts as the medium through which ions migrate between the anode and cathode. This migration process inherently involves the absorption and release of ions by the metal phosphide anode, resulting in volume expansion and the formation of various intermediates, which in turn affect the electrochemical properties of the material. The addition of electrolyte additives is often studied to determine whether they contribute to the excellent cycling performance of phosphides.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0114" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0114_R_d140478325e4962" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 114 - Sci. Rep.">114</a>, <a href="#smll202310426-bib-0202" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0202_R_d140478325e4962" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 202 - J. Mater. Chem. A">202</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Liu et&nbsp;al. synthesized Zn<sub>0.5</sub>Ge<sub>0.5</sub>P, using 1 M NaPF<sub>6</sub> in diglyme or 1&nbsp;<span class="smallCaps">m</span> NaClO<sub>4</sub> in EC/DMC/FEC as electrolytes.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0097" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0097_R_d140478325e4978" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 97 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">97</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In the early stage of SEI formation, the diffusion rate of Na<sup>+</sup> in the diglyme-induced SEI is faster than that of EC/DMC/FEC. Moreover, when compared to electrolytes based on esters, Zn<sub>0.5</sub>Ge<sub>0.5</sub>P in ether-based electrolytes exhibits superior capacity retention due to the thinner and more stable solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) layer formed in the ether-based electrolyte. The results show that stable SEI is beneficial to the cyclic properties of Zn<sub>0.5</sub>Ge<sub>0.5</sub>P, and rapid charge transfer is beneficial to the magnification properties of Zn<sub>0.5</sub>Ge<sub>0.5</sub>P. The effects of different types of carbonate (EC and DMC mixture) or diglyme electrolyte on the electrochemical properties of SIBs were investigated. It is found that the latter has the effect of higher capacity, longer cycle life, and smaller polarization. Ether electrolyte has a wide temperature window and better reduction stability, which is conducive to SEI formation, thus extending the cycle life. Thus, electrode expansion/shrinkage of the electrode during cycling is fairly constant in the diglyme electrolyte, whereas rapid fading is observed in the carbonate electrolyte.</p>
            </section>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="smll202310426-sec-0220">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="smll202310426-sec-0220-title">5 Conclusion and Outlook</h2>
         
         <p>In this paper, the synthesis methods of metal phosphides and the research progress of metal phosphide applications in SIBs in recent years are reviewed. Phosphorus is a promising anode material for SIBs due to its low cost and high theoretical capacity. Metal phosphide has high energy storage because of its high energy density. The metal phosphide has good reaction performance with sodium ions. Because of its structure, it can stably store and release sodium ions, thereby improving the performance of SIBs.</p>
         
         <div class="paragraph-element">However, metal phosphide also has its own defects, which make its actual capacity much lower than the theoretical capacity and limited cycle life. First of all, there is a serious volume expansion problem of metal phosphide in the process of sodium insertion/extraction reaction. Therefore, the capacity of metal phosphide is low. In addition, the reaction mechanism of metal phosphide in SIBs is still unclear. Researchers have mostly focused on the research and development of high-capacity and high-performance electrode materials and the optimization of synthetic parameters. But there is a lack of studies on material properties, reaction kinetics, and electrochemical reaction mechanisms. In order to solve the above problems, we summarize the following strategies:

            <ol start="1" class="">
               
               <li>
                  <p>By adjusting the size and structure of the anode material or combining it with other materials, the shortcomings of capacity decay during the cycle of metal phosphide can be effectively overcome. Reducing the particle size to the nanometer level can not only improve the electrochemical activity of metal phosphide but also shorten the diffusion distance of sodium ions, so as to improve the electrochemical performance of metal phosphide. The common method is doping C, graphene, and other conductive matrix. On the one hand, it can improve the conductivity of the material and provide high-speed channels for the transport of ions and electrons. On the other hand, by constructing a pore, hollow, 3D framework or core-shell structure, the agglomeration of particles is inhibited and the volume expansion is reduced. The specific capacity can also be improved by doping elements such as S and Se to adjust the charge density distribution and increase the active site. These methods have shown the potential to solve the problem of cycle capacity decay, demonstrating the versatility and adaptability of metal phosphide in various configurations. In addition to the above methods, we believe that amorphous metal phosphide should be paid attention to. The amorphous structure, with its inherent isotropy and loose framework that are conducive to energy storage, is expected to significantly reduce volume change in reversible transformation reactions and effectively release volume strain, thereby enhancing structural integrity. Moreover, the internal disorder of amorphous materials can greatly reduce the charge transport resistance and improve the ability of amorphous materials to carry charge carriers, especially large sodium ions. First-principles calculations show that amorphous materials exhibit lower Gibbs free energy than crystalline materials, which indicates better reversibility of the transformation reaction. Therefore, amorphous materials can provide a more stable structure and faster charge transfer, thereby improving cycle stability and enhancing the electrochemical performance of the material. However, it is difficult to control the structure of amorphous nanomaterials because of the metastable and long-range disorder of their internal structures.</p>
                  </li>
               
               <li>
                  <p>A suitable synthesis method will make metal phosphide form a stable structure to restrain volume expansion and improve cycle performance. So far, the methods of preparing metal phosphide materials include HEBM, hydrothermal solvothermal, chemical vapor deposition, phosphatization, and so on. However, these methods have inherent limitations that limit their further application. We prepared metal phosphide composite carbon skeletons by using MOF as the precursor and sealing MOF with P in a quartz tube under vacuum and high-temperature conditions.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202310426-bib-0203" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202310426-bib-0203_R_d140478325e5020" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 203 - Dalton Trans.">203</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The metal phosphide synthesized with MOF as the precursor has good dispersibility and non-agglomeration. The carbon generated by the organic ligands in MOF increases the electrical conductivity of the material. The existence of the C framework can effectively solve the agglomeration problem in the synthesis process and alleviate the serious volume expansion during the cycle. The cyclic performance of the material is greatly improved. This method is easy to operate and has high repeatability. However, the method requires further characterization to determine the specific structure and chemical formula. In addition, we believe that plasma-assisted synthesis of transition metal phosphide (TMP) theoretically has the potential to significantly increase activity. Due to the high reactivity of the plasma, this reaction allows rapid synthesis (from 30&nbsp;s to 20&nbsp;min) of TMP at low temperatures (100–300&nbsp;°C). The rapid formation of TMP could lead to the introduction of a large number of defects in the nanostructure of TMP. These defects may play a useful role in electrochemical energy storage systems. Specifically, the presence of defects in the nanostructures can effectively inhibit the volume expansion during charging and discharging and reduce the internal stresses in the battery, enabling improved cycling stability and lifetime.</p>
                  </li>
               
               <li>
                  <p>In situ X-ray diffraction, in situ electron microscopy, and other advanced in situ characterization techniques are used to further analyze and refine the reaction path of Na and P in the process of sodium insertion/extraction of metal phosphide, including the evolution path of various Na-P intermediates in the process of sodium insertion and extraction and the electrochemical principle behind it. More comprehensive in situ technical studies are needed in order to reveal the structural change behavior of phosphide during charging/discharging, including the mechanism of sodium storage and the principle of volume expansion. This can guide the design of the material structure and thus help to improve the electrochemical performance of the metal phosphide.</p>
                  </li>
               
               <li>
                  <p>In addition to the design of electrode materials, electrolyte additives also play an important role in battery performance. Electrolyte additives are considered to be an effective way to form a stable SEI layer and affect the cycling properties of metal phosphide. For example, the electrolyte additive FEC can promote the formation of dense SEI and effectively inhibit electrolyte decomposition, thereby improving the specific capacity and cycle performance of the battery. Ether electrolyte is also conducive to SEI formation, thus prolonging the cycle life. But very little research has been done on them. Therefore, the mechanism of action of these components in the metal phosphide anode material system needs to be further investigated.</p>
                  </li>
               </ol>
         </div>
         
         <p>In conclusion, the application of metal phosphide in SIBs has made good progress. In the future, the mechanism and volume change of sodium storage need to be further explored and studied. In order to suppress the volume change and improve the conductivity, researchers need to work tirelessly to come up with better methods and designs. It is foreseeable that metal phosphide material will promote the application and development of SIBs.</p>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="smll202310426-sec-0230-title"> Acknowledgements</h2>

         <ol></ol>
      </div>

                  <li data-bib-id="smll202310426-bib-0004"><span class="bullet">4</span><span class="author">Z. Zhang</span>, <span class="author">N. Song</span>, <span class="author">J. Wang</span>, <span class="author">Y. Liu</span>, <span class="author">Z. Dai</span>, <span class="author">G.
